If not done no new events will be emitted for this key.\\n46: // If an event handling is marked as failed the configured error handler is called\\n47: // (WithErrorHandler). The default error handler will requeue the event (by its key) for\\n48: // later retried processing. The requeueing is rate limited and can be configured with\\n49: // WithRateLimiter option to Events().\\n50: //\\n51: // The resource is lazy, e.g. it will not start the informer until a call\\n52: // has been made to Events() or Store().\\n53: type Resource[T k8sRuntime.Object] interface {\\n54: \\t// Resource can be observed either via Observe() or via Events(). The observable\\n55: \\t// is implemented in terms of Events() and same semantics apply.\\n56: \\tstream.Observable[Event[T]]\\n57: \\n58: \\t// Events returns a channel of events. Each event must be marked as handled\\n59: \\t// with a call to Done() which marks the key processed. No new events for this key\\n60: \\t// will be emitted before Done() is called.\\n61: \\t//\\n62: \\t// A missing Done() will lead to an eventual panic (via finalizer on Event[T]).\\n63: \\t// Panic on this situation is needed as otherwise no new events would be emitted\\n64: \\t// and thus this needs to be enforced.\\n65: \\t//\\n66: \\t// A stream of Upsert events are emitted first to replay the current state of the\\n67: \\t// store after which incremental upserts and deletes follow until the underlying\\n68: \\t// store is synchronized after which a Sync event is emitted and further incremental\\n69: \\t// updates:\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t//\\t(start observing), Upsert, Upsert, Upsert, (done replaying store contents), Upsert, Upsert,\\n72: \\t//\\t  (store synchronized with API server), Sync, Upsert, Delete, Upsert, ...\\n73: \\t//\\n74: \\t// The emitting of the Sync event does not depend on whether or not Upsert events have\\n75: \\t// all been marked Done() without an error. The sync event solely signals that the underlying\\n76: \\t// store has synchronized and that Upsert events for objects in a synchronized store have been\\n77: \\t// sent to the observer.\\n78: \\t//\\n79: \\t// When Done() is called with non-nil error the error handler is invoked, which\\n80: \\t// can ignore, requeue the event (by key) or close the channel. The default error handler\\n81: \\t// will requeue.\\n82: \\t//\\n83: \\t// If an Upsert is retried and the object has been deleted, a Delete event will be emitted instead.\\n84: \\t// Conversely if a Delete event is retried and the object has been recreated with the same key,\\n85: \\t// an Upsert will be emitted instead.\\n86: \\t//\\n87: \\t// If an objects is created and immediately deleted, then a slow observer may not observe this at\\n88: \\t// all. In all cases a Delete event is only emitted if the observer has seen an Upsert. Whether or\\n89: \\t// not it had been successfully handled (via Done(nil)) does not affect this property.\\n90: \\tEvents(ctx context.Context, opts ...EventsOpt) <-chan Event[T]\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Store retrieves the read-only store for the resource. Blocks until\\n93: \\t// the store has been synchronized or the context cancelled.\\n94: \\t// Returns a non-nil error if context is cancelled or the resource\\n95: \\t// has been stopped before store has synchronized.\\n96: \\tStore(context.Context) (Store[T], error)\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // New creates a new Resource[T]. Use with hive.Provide:\\n100: //\\n101: //\\tvar exampleCell = hive.Module(\\n102: //\\t\\t\\\"example\\\",\\n103: //\\t \\tcell.Provide(\\n104: //\\t\\t \\t// Provide `Resource[*slim_corev1.Pod]` to //\\t)\\n114: //\\n115: //\\tfunc usePods(pods resource.Resource[*slim_corev1.Pod]) {\\n116: //\\t\\tgo func() {\\n117: //\\t\\t\\tfor ev := range podEvents {\\n118: //\\t\\t   \\t\\tonPodEvent(ev)\\n119: //\\t\\t   \\t}\\n120: //\\t\\t}\\n121: //\\t\\treturn e\\n122: //\\t}\\n123: //\\tfunc onPodEvent(event resource.Event[*slim_core.Pod]) {\\n124: //\\t\\tswitch event.Kind {\\n125: //\\t\\tcase resource.Sync:\\n126: //\\t\\t\\t// Pods have now been synced and the set of Upsert events\\n127: //\\t\\t\\t// received thus far forms a coherent snapshot.\\n128: //\\n129: The requeueing is rate limited and can be configured with\\n49: // WithRateLimiter option to Events().\\n50: //\\n51: // The resource is lazy, e.g. it will not start the informer until a call\\n52: // has been made to Events() or Store().\\n53: type Resource[T k8sRuntime.Object] interface {\\n54: \\t// Resource can be observed either via Observe() or via Events(). The sync event solely signals that the underlying\\n76: \\t// store has synchronized and that Upsert events for objects in a synchronized store have been\\n77: \\t// sent to the observer.\\n78: \\t//\\n79: \\t// When Done() is called with non-nil error the error handler is invoked, which\\n80: \\t// can ignore, requeue the event (by key) or close the channel. The default error handler\\n81: \\t// will requeue.\\n82: \\t//\\n83: \\t// If an Upsert is retried and the object has been deleted, a Delete event will be emitted instead.\\n84: \\t// Conversely if a Delete event is retried and the object has been recreated with the same key,\\n85: \\t// an Upsert will be emitted instead.\\n86: \\t//\\n87: \\t// If an objects is created and immediately deleted, then a slow observer may not observe this at\\n88: \\t// all. Whether or\\n89: \\t// not it had been successfully handled (via Done(nil)) does not affect this property.\\n90: \\tEvents(ctx context.Context, opts ...EventsOpt) <-chan Event[T]\\n91: \\n92: \\t// Store retrieves the read-only store for the resource. Blocks until\\n93: \\t// the store has been synchronized or the context cancelled.\\n94: \\t// Returns a non-nil error if context is cancelled or the resource\\n95: \\t// has been stopped before store has synchronized.\\n96: \\tStore(context.Context) (Store[T], error)\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: // New creates a new Resource[T].            logrus.FieldLogger\n\tmaxPerNamespace    int\n\tpolicyCounts       map[string]int\n\tmu                 sync.RWMutex\n\tcnpResource        resource.Resource[*cilium_v2.CiliumNetworkPolicy]\n\tquotaResource      resource.Resource[*cilium_v2.CiliumPolicyQuota]\n}\n\n// NewPolicyQuotaController creates a new PolicyQuotaController.\nfunc cnpResource,\n\t\tquotaResource:   quotaResource,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Run starts the controller's event loop.\nfunc (c *PolicyQuotaController) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\tc.log.Info(\"Starting PolicyQuotaController\")\n\tdefer c.log.Info(\"Stopped PolicyQuotaController\")\n\n\tcnpEvents := c.cnpResource.Events(ctx)\n\tquotaEvents := c.quotaResource.Events(ctx)\n\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect c.policyCounts[ns]).\n\t\t\tDebug(\"CiliumNetworkPolicy deleted, decremented namespace count\")\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (c *PolicyQuotaController) handleQuotaEvent(event resource.Event[*cilium_v2.CiliumPolicyQuota]) {\n\tdefer event.Done(nil)\n\n\tif event.Kind == resource.Sync {\n\t\tc.log.Debug(\"CiliumPolicyQuota sync event received\")\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tns := resource.Delete:\n\t\tc.log.\n\t\t\tWithField(\"namespace\", ns).\n\t\t\tDebug(\"CiliumPolicyQuota deleted, quota enforcement disabled for namespace\")\n\t}\n}\n\n// CheckQuota checks if adding a new So EventsOpt is a function type. My mock implementation doesn't need to do anything with the opts since it's just a test mock. Let me verify the final structure by checking if there are any edge cases I might have missed.Looking at my implementation again, I notice one potential issue: when handling CNP events, if the policy is upserted, I increment the count immediately. However, in a real scenario, we might want to check if the policy already exists (e.g., if it's an update vs a creation). But looking at the resource.Event API, the Kind tells us whether it's an Upsert or Delete, and Upsert covers both creation and updates.The current implementation increments on every Upsert, which means:- First Upsert: count goes from 0 to 1\n- Second Upsert (update of same policy): count goes from 1 to 2 (this is incorrect!)\n\nThis is a bug! I need to track which policies exist in each namespace to avoid double-counting. However, looking at the requirements again, I see that the requirements say:- \"Per-namespace counting using a thread-safe map\"- \"CheckQuota method that returns error if quota exceeded\"There's no mention of tracking individual policies. But the event handling should probably track if the event is a creation or an update.Actually, looking more carefully at the resource.Event handling pattern, I think the issue is that Upsert events don't distinguish between Creates and Updates. So when we get an Upsert for a policy that already exists, we should not increment the count again.\n\nLet me think about this more carefully. In a real Kubernetes controller, we would get:1. Initial sync events with all existing resources2. Then Upsert events for new resources or updated resources3. Delete events when resources are deletedIf we're implementing a controller that watches events, we should be tracking the actual state of the cluster. via `policyExists` map to avoid double-counting on updates\n- **Run(ctx context.Context)** method implementing the controller event loop\n- **CheckQuota(namespace string) error** method that returns `QuotaExceededError` if quota exceeded\n- **GetPolicyCount(namespace string) int** helper method\n- **Event handling** for both CiliumNetworkPolicy and CiliumPolicyQuota resources\n- **Structured logging** using Cilium's logfields pattern\n- **Proper event cleanup** with defer event.Done(nil) pattern\n\n**Implementation Details:**\n- Watches both CiliumNetworkPolicy (to count policies) and CiliumPolicyQuota (for quota configuration) resources\n- Handles Upsert events by checking if policy already exists before incrementing count\n- Handles Delete events by decrementing count if policy was tracked\n- Handles Sync events to complete initial synchronization\n\n### 4. **Comprehensive Tests** (`pkg/policy/quota/controller_test.go`)\n\n**Test Coverage:**\n- Constructor creation\n- error message format\n\n**Test Infrastructure:**\n- Mock resource implementation for testing\n- Event channel-based communication\n- Done callback pattern matching Cilium's resource API\n\n### Architecture Decisions\n\n1. **Dual-tracking approach**: Maintains both count and individual policy names to distinguish between creates and updates, preventing quota miscounts\n2. **Resource.Resource pattern**: Uses Cilium's standard `resource.Resource[T]` interface for watching Kubernetes resources\n3. **Thread-safe operations**: All modifications to shared state protected by RWMutex\n4. **Event-driven design**: Follows Cilium's event-loop pattern for reactive resource management\n5. **Proper error types**: Custom `QuotaExceededError` for detailed quota violation information\n\nAll
